My template making doesn't produce the perfect templates. It disallows more combinations than needed.
For example., with the Andromeda chain, my template requires (5,0) and (2,2) to be different, but the
supplied chain to get the template has both of those as the same colour. This is because my method
find groups of puyo that pop together and labels them with unique capital letters. The group of yellows
at the beginning actually split up and pop in separate groups, so they consist of different capital letters
and my relationship matrix makes capital letters that are adjacent at any point in the chain different colours
to each other (in case that they accidentally pop) and this is probably too cautious. This means that those 2 coordinates
have to be different colours even though they don't have to be.

I made TMS look for the node that has the highest accordance score, rather than just the depth-3 nodes.
This will result in a more greedy algorithm that looks for more early payoffs. It may not be a good change, however
it ensures that the chain gets finished if it is nearing the finish. And then switches to PMS.

So, currently the TMS holds a tree very similar to PMS depth-3, where if a node causes a chain, then it doesn't have children.
However, this sometimes doesn't allow my templates to even be finished. I think it may be better to allow chains to exist in the
tree and then also have children to the resulting board state. Or maybe have the board state for the chaining board to be the
actual resulting board state (however, there will be the problem of finding the move that resulted in that board state).
This will allow TMS to get rid of puyo that it doesn't need in small chains to then reach the finished template.
Another thing to consider is adding a small incentive to not fill up the board unnecessarily. So a heuristic could be used
to decrease the quality of an accordance score by how much the board is filled up (like a secondary score that it takes
into consideration).

I've noticed that PMS may not be the best thing after TMS. After TMS, the board may be extremely messy and the trigger to the chain
may be buried under puyo and so PMS may not even know there is a chain there and may just fill up the board instead. To alleviate this,
I have two ideas: I could custom make an algorithm that searches for the TMS chain trigger and unburies it to set it off, or
I could add incentive in the template to leave the trigger unburied and open to then allow PMS to see it and build off it. I will
try the second approach.

I've added another csv file for each template where it shows the start of the chain, or the coordinates where the chain
could be set off. By specifying the coordinates, I can then check if any move blocks these spaces before the
chain is finished. I want the algorithm to avoid these spaces as much as possible. I still need to think about how
this should be done.
